   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    World oil market chronology from 2003
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>

           worldwide view
          </a>
          of the subject
         </b>

     <dl>
      <dd>
       <i>
        This article is a chronology of events affecting the oil market. For a discussion of the energy crisis of the same period, see
        <a href="/wiki/2000s_energy_crisis" title="2000s energy crisis">
         2000s energy crisis
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effects_of_2000s_energy_crisis" title="Effects of 2000s energy crisis">
         Effects of 2000s energy crisis
        </a>
        . For current fuel prices see
        <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_and_diesel_usage_and_pricing" title="Gasoline and diesel usage and pricing">
         Gasoline usage and pricing
        </a>
        .
       </i>
      </dd>

      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brent_Spot_monthly.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="1108" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Brent_Spot_monthly.svg/300px-Brent_Spot_monthly.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Brent_Spot_monthly.svg/450px-Brent_Spot_monthly.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Brent_Spot_monthly.svg/600px-Brent_Spot_monthly.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">

         </a>
        </div>
        Medium term
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Price_of_petroleum" title="Price of petroleum">
         Brent oil prices
        </a>
        since May 1987
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crude_oil_price_WTI_EIA_since_2000.svg">

       </a>

        </a>
        prices for West Texas Intermediate since 2000, monthly overlaid on daily prices to show the variation
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2480" data-file-width="3508" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png/350px-Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png/525px-Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png/700px-Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png 2x" width="350"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crude_oil_prices_in_dollar_and_euro.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Oil prices for Brent in US$ (blue) and Euro (red)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      From the mid-1980s to September 2003, the inflation adjusted price of a
      <a href="/wiki/Barrel_(unit)" title="Barrel (unit)">
       barrel
      </a>
      of crude oil on
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mercantile_Exchange" title="New York Mercantile Exchange">
       NYMEX
      </a>
      was generally under $25/barrel. Then, during 2004, the price rose above $40, and then $50. A series of events led the price to exceed $60 by August 11, 2005, leading to a record-speed hike that reached $75 by the middle of 2006. Prices then dropped back to $60/barrel by the early part of 2007 before rising steeply again to $92/barrel by October 2007, and $99.29/barrel for December futures in
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
       New York
      </a>
      on November 21, 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Throughout the first half of 2008, oil regularly reached record high prices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Prices on June 27, 2008, touched $141.71/barrel, for August delivery in the New York Mercantile Exchange, amid
      <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
       Libya
      </a>
      's threat to cut output, and
      <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">
       OPEC
      </a>
      's president predicted prices may reach $170 by the
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">
       Northern
      </a>
      summer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The highest recorded price per barrel maximum of $147.02 was reached on July 11, 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After falling below $100 in the late summer of 2008, prices rose again in late September. On September 22, oil rose over $25 to $130 before settling again to $120.92, marking a record one-day gain of $16.37. Electronic crude oil trading was temporarily halted by NYMEX when the daily price rise limit of $10 was reached, but the limit was reset seconds later and trading resumed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By October 16, prices had fallen again to below $70, and on November 6 oil closed below $60.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-money.cnn.com_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-money.cnn.com-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Then in 2009, prices went slightly higher, although not to the extent of the 2005-2007 crisis, exceeding $100 in 2011 and most of 2012. Since late 2013 the oil price has fallen below the $100 mark, plummeting below the $50 mark one year later.
     </p>
     <p>
      As the price of producing petroleum did not rise significantly, the price increases have coincided with a period of record profits for the oil industry.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Between 2004 and 2007, the profits of the six
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supermajor" title="Supermajor">
       supermajors
      </a>
      -
      <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">
       ExxonMobil
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." title="Total S.A.">
       Total
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">
       Shell
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">
       BP
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">
       Chevron
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/ConocoPhillips" title="ConocoPhillips">
       ConocoPhillips
      </a>
      - totaled $494.8 billion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Likewise, major oil-dependent countries such as
      <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
       Saudi Arabia
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">
       United Arab Emirates
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
       Canada
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
       Russia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
       Venezuela
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
       Nigeria
      </a>
      have benefited economically from surging oil prices during the 2000s.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2003">
       2003
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: 2003">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      crude oil prices averaged $30 a barrel in 2003 due to political instability within various oil producing nations. It rose 19% from the average in 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">
       2003 invasion of Iraq
      </a>
      marked a significant event for oil markets because
      <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">
       Iraq
      </a>
      contains a large amount of global
      <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">
       oil reserves
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The conflict coincided with an increase in global demand for petroleum, but it also reduced Iraq's current oil production and has been blamed for increasing oil prices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collier_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Collier-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, oil company CEO
      <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Simmons" title="Matthew Simmons">
       Matthew Simmons
      </a>
      emphasizes the
      <a href="/wiki/Peak_oil" title="Peak oil">
       peaking and decline
      </a>
      of oil-exporting in
      <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
       Mexico
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      is the reason for the
      <a href="/wiki/Price_gouging" title="Price gouging">
       price gouging
      </a>
      . According to Simmons,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-simmons_another_nail_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-simmons_another_nail-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      isolated events, such as the Iraq war, affect short-term prices but do not determine a long-term trend. Simmons cites the use of
      <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_oil_recovery" title="Enhanced oil recovery">
       enhanced oil recovery
      </a>
      techniques in large fields such as Mexico's
      <a href="/wiki/Cantarell_Field" title="Cantarell Field">
       Cantarell
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-simmons_another_nail_15-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-simmons_another_nail-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      which maintained production for a few years until it eventually declined. Pumping oil out of Iraq may reduce petroleum prices in the short term, but will be unable to perpetually lower the price. From Simmons' point of view, the invasion of Iraq is associated with the start of long-term increase in oil prices, but it may
      <a href="/wiki/Mitigation_of_peak_oil" title="Mitigation of peak oil">
       mitigate the decline
      </a>
      in oil production by retaining a partial amount of Iraq's oil reserves. As a direct consequence, the oil production capacity was diminished to 2 million barrels (320,000 m
      <sup>
       3
      </sup>
      ) per day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ibrahim_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ibrahim-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2004_to_2008:_rising_costs_of_oil">
       2004 to 2008: rising costs of oil
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2004 to 2008: rising costs of oil">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gas_prices,_July_2006,_San_Francisco,_California_01.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Gas_prices%2C_July_2006%2C_San_Francisco%2C_California_01.jpg/220px-Gas_prices%2C_July_2006%2C_San_Francisco%2C_California_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Gas_prices%2C_July_2006%2C_San_Francisco%2C_California_01.jpg/330px-Gas_prices%2C_July_2006%2C_San_Francisco%2C_California_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Gas_prices%2C_July_2006%2C_San_Francisco%2C_California_01.jpg/440px-Gas_prices%2C_July_2006%2C_San_Francisco%2C_California_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gas_prices,_July_2006,_San_Francisco,_California_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        July 2006,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" title="San Francisco, California">
         San Francisco
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
         California
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After retreating for several months in late 2004 and early 2005,
      <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
       crude oil
      </a>
      prices rose to new highs in March 2005. The price on
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mercantile_Exchange" title="New York Mercantile Exchange">
       NYMEX
      </a>
      has been above
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
       $
      </a>
      50 per barrel since March 5, 2005. In June 2005, crude oil prices broke the psychological barrier of $60 per barrel.
     </p>
     <p>
      From 2005 onwards, the price elasticity of the crude oil market changed significantly. Before 2005 a small increase in oil price lead to an noticeable expansion of the production volume. Later price rises let the production grow only by small numbers. This was the reason to call 2005 a tipping point.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        [17]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After the destruction of
      <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">
       Hurricane Katrina
      </a>
      in the United States, gasoline prices reached a record high during the first week of September 2005. The average retail price was, on average,
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
       $
      </a>
      3.04 per U.S. gallon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The average retail price of a liter of
      <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">
       petrol
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      was 86.4p on October 19, 2006, or $6.13 per gallon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Oil production in Iraq continued to decline as result of the nation's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_war_in_Iraq_(2006-07)" title="Civil war in Iraq (2006-07)">
       ongoing conflict
      </a>
      causing a decrease in production to 1 million barrels per day (160,000 m
      <sup>
       3
      </sup>
      /d).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krane_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Krane-20">
        [20]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In mid-2006, crude oil was traded for over USD 79 per
      <a href="/wiki/Barrel#Oil_barrel" title="Barrel">
       barrel (bbl)
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        [21]
       </a>
      </sup>
      setting an all-time record. The run-up is attributed to a 1.9 increase in gasoline consumption, geopolitical tensions resulting from
      <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">
       North Korea
      </a>
      's missile launch. The ongoing Iraq war, as well as
      <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">
       Israel and Lebanon going to war
      </a>
      are also causative factors. The higher price of oil substantially cut growth of world oil demand in 2006, including a reduction in oil demand of the
      <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">
       OECD
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        [22]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After news of North Korea's successful nuclear test on October 9, 2006, oil prices rose past $60 a barrel, but fell back the next day.
     </p>
     <p>
      On October 19, 2007, U.S.
      <a href="/wiki/Light_crude_oil" title="Light crude oil">
       light crude
      </a>
      rose to $90.02 per barrel due to a combination of ongoing tensions in eastern
      <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
       Turkey
      </a>
      and the reducing strength of the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
       U.S. dollar
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Prices fell briefly on the expectation of increased U.S. crude oil stocks, however they quickly rose to a peak of $92.22 on October 26, 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        [24]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On January 2, 2008, U.S.
      <a href="/wiki/Light_crude_oil" title="Light crude oil">
       light crude
      </a>
      surpassed $100 per barrel before falling to $99.69 due to tensions on New Years Day in
      <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
       Nigeria
      </a>
      , and on suspicion that U.S. crude stocks will have dropped for the seventh consecutive week. A
      <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">
       BBC
      </a>
      report from the following day stated a single trader bid up the price; Stephen Schork, a former floor trader on the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mercantile_Exchange" title="New York Mercantile Exchange">
       New York Mercantile Exchange
      </a>
      and the editor of an oil market newsletter, said one
      <a href="/wiki/Floor_trader" title="Floor trader">
       floor trader
      </a>
      bought 1,000 barrels (160 m
      <sup>
       3
      </sup>
      ), the smallest amount permitted, and immediately sold it for $99.40 at a $600 loss.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Oil fell back later in the week to $97.91 at the close of trading on Friday, January 4, in part due to a weak jobs report that showed unemployment had risen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        [26]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On March 5, 2008,
      <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">
       OPEC
      </a>
      accused the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
       United States
      </a>
      of economic "mismanagement" that was pushing oil prices to record highs, rebuffing calls to boost output and laying blame at the
      <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">
       George W. Bush administration
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Oil prices surged above $110 to a new inflation-adjusted record on March 12, 2008 before settling at $109.92.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On April 18, 2008 the price of oil broke $117 per barrel after a Nigerian militant group claimed an attack on an oil pipeline.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Oil prices rose to a new high of $119.90 a barrel on April 22, 2008,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
      before dipping and then rising $3 on April 25, 2008 to $119.10 on the New York Mercantile Exchange after a news report that a ship contracted by the U.S. Military Sealift Command fired at an Iranian boat.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 6, prices rose $11 in 24 hours, the largest gain in history due to the possibility of an Israeli attack on Iran.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The combination of two major oil suppliers reducing supply generated fears of a repeat of the
      <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">
       1973 oil crisis
      </a>
      . The mid-July decision of Saudi Arabia to increase oil output caused little significant influence on prices. According to the oil minister of the Islamic Republic of Iran, Gholam-Hossein Nozari, the world markets were saturated
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a Saudi promise of increased production would not lower prices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several Asian refineries were refusing Saudi petroleum in late June because they were over priced
      <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_(crude_oil)" title="Benchmark (crude oil)">
       grade
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-press1_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-press1-35">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 3, "the
      <a href="/wiki/Brent_Crude" title="Brent Crude">
       Brent North Sea
      </a>
      crude contract for August delivery rose to $US145.01 a barrel" in Asian trade.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
      London Brent crude reached a record of $145.75 a barrel, and Brent crude for August delivery peaked to a record $145.11 a barrel on London's ICE Futures Europe exchange, and to $144.44 a barrel on the NYMExchange.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By midday in Europe, crude rose to $145.85 a barrel on the NYME while Brent crude futures rose to a trading record of $146.69 a barrel on the ICE Futures exchange.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        [40]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2008:_oil_prices_peak_at_.24145.85_then_bottom_at_.2432">
       2008: oil prices peak at $145.85 then bottom at $32
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2008: oil prices peak at $145.85 then bottom at $32">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG/220px-March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG/330px-March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG/440px-March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:March_2009_NJ_Gas_Prices.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        March 2009,
        <a href="/wiki/Dunellen,_New_Jersey" title="Dunellen, New Jersey">
         Dunellen
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
         New Jersey
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On July 15, 2008, a bubble-bursting sell-off began after remarks by President Bush the previous day that the ban on oil drilling would be lifted.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This precipitated an $8 drop, the biggest since
      <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">
       the first US-Iraq war
      </a>
      . By the end of the week, crude oil fell 11% to $128, also affected by easing of tensions between the US and Iran.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By August 13, prices had fallen to $113 a barrel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the middle of September, oil price fell below $100 for the first time in over six months,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
      falling below $92 in the aftermath of the
      <a href="/wiki/Lehman_Brothers" title="Lehman Brothers">
       Lehman Brothers
      </a>
      bankruptcy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A stronger US dollar and a likely decline in European demand were suggested to be among the causes of the decline.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By October 24, the price of crude dropped to $64.15,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and closed at $60.77 on November 6.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-money.cnn.com_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-money.cnn.com-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the end of December, 2008, oil had bottomed out at $32.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2009">
       2009
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2009">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In January 2009, oil prices rose temporarily because of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932009_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2008–2009 Israel–Gaza conflict">
       tensions in the Gaza Strip
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      From mid January to February 13, oil fell to near $35 a barrel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2010">
       2010
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2010">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      On May 21, 2010, the price of oil had dropped in two weeks from $88 to $70 mainly due to concerns over how European countries would reduce budget deficits; if the European economy slowed down, this would mean less demand for crude oil. Also, if the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_European_sovereign_debt_crisis" title="2010 European sovereign debt crisis">
       European economic crisis
      </a>
      caused the American economy to have problems, demand for oil would be reduced further.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        [50]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other factors included the strong
      <a href="/wiki/Dollar" title="Dollar">
       dollar
      </a>
      and high inventories. According to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Energy_Information_Administration" title="U.S. Energy Information Administration">
       U.S. Energy Information Administration
      </a>
      , gas prices nationwide averaged $2.91 on May 10, dropping to $2.79 two weeks later. The
      <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill">
       Deepwater Horizon oil spill
      </a>
      was not a factor in gas prices since the well had not produced.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        [51]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Prices rose back to $90/barrel in December 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        [52]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The US average for a gallon of 87 octane regular unleaded averaged $3.00/gallon on December 23, sparking fear of a second recession if prices reached $100/barrel and $4.00/gallon gasoline, as forecasted for spring 2011.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The price increases in December were based on global demand and the Arctic blasts affecting
      <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
       North America
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_of_2010%E2%80%932011_in_Europe" title="Winter of 2010–2011 in Europe">
       Europe
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2011">
       2011
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2011">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">
       Political turmoil
      </a>
      in Egypt, Libya, Yemen, and Bahrain drove oil prices to $95/barrel in late February 2011. A few days prior, oil prices on the NYMEX closed at $86. Oil prices topped at $103 on February 24 where oil production is curtailed to the political upheaval in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_civil_war" title="2011 Libyan civil war">
       Libya
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        [53]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Oil supplies remained high, and Saudi Arabia assured an increase in production to counteract shutdowns. Still, the Mideast and North African crisis led to a rise in oil prices to the highest level in two years, with gasoline prices following. Though most Libyan oil went to Europe, all oil prices reacted. The average price of gasoline in the United States increased 6 cents to $3.17.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        [54]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On March 1, 2011, a significant drop in Libyan production and fears of more instability in other countries pushed the price of oil over $100 a barrel in New York trading, while the average price of gas reached $3.37. Despite Saudi promises, the
      <a href="/wiki/Sour_crude_oil" title="Sour crude oil">
       sour type oil
      </a>
      the country exported could not replace the more desirable
      <a href="/wiki/Sweet_crude_oil" title="Sweet crude oil">
       sweet Libyan oil
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        [55]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On March 7, 2011, the average price of gas having reached $3.57, individuals were making changes in their driving.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        [56]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The weakened U.S. Dollar resulted in a spike to $112/barrel with the national average of $3.74/gallon - with expectations of damaging the U.S. economy suggestive of a long-term recession.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        [57]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of April 26, the national average was $3.87 - with a fear of $4/gallon as the nationwide average prior to the summer driving season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        [58]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The national average rose on May 5, 2011 for the 44th straight day, reaching $3.98. However, that same day,
      <a href="/wiki/West_Texas_Intermediate" title="West Texas Intermediate">
       West Texas Intermediate
      </a>
      crude fell below $100 a barrel, the lowest since March 16.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        [59]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This came after crude oil for June delivery reached $114.83 on May 2, the highest since September 2008, before closing at $97.18 on May 6, a day after dropping 9 percent, the most dramatic single-day drop in over two years. Gas prices fell slightly on May 6, and experts predicted $3.50 a gallon by summer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        [61]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In mid-June, West Texas Intermediate crude for July delivery fell nearly $2 to $93.01, the lowest price since February. The dollar was up and the
      <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
       euro
      </a>
      and other currencies down, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_sovereign_debt_crisis" title="European sovereign debt crisis">
       European economic crisis
      </a>
      made investors concerned. London
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brent_crude" title="Brent crude">
       Brent crude
      </a>
      fell 81 cents to $113.21. On June 15 the Energy Information Association said oil consumption was down 3.5 percent from a year earlier, but wholesale gasoline demand was up for the first time in several weeks. The price of gas on June 17 was $3.67.5 a gallon, 25.1 cents lower than a month earlier but 96.8 cents above a year earlier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        [63]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On June 24, the price of gas was $3.62.8 and expected to go much lower due to the opening of the
      <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Petroleum_Reserve_(United_States)" title="Strategic Petroleum Reserve (United States)">
       Strategic Petroleum Reserve
      </a>
      . U.S. oil prices fell below $90 before rising again, and Brent crude fell two percent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        [64]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, on June 29, West Texas intermediate crude had risen to $94.96, almost $5 above the lowest point reached after the previous week's action. One reason was the falling dollar, as Greece appeared less likely to default on its debt; concern over the Greek debt crisis had caused falling oil prices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        [65]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        [66]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After another week, oil for August delivery had risen from $90.61 to $98.67 and gas prices were up five cents. Increased worldwide demand was one reason.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        [67]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Brent_Crude" title="Brent Crude">
       Brent Crude
      </a>
      remained high at $118.38 partly due to supply problems in Europe, including lower
      <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">
       North Sea
      </a>
      production and the continuing war in Libya.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        [68]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On August 4, the price of oil dropped 6 percent to its lowest level in 6 months. On August 5, the price had dropped $8.82 in a week to $86.88 per barrel on the New York Mercantile Exchange. The same pessimistic economic news that caused stock prices to fall also decreased expected energy demand, and experts predicted a gas price drop of 35 cents per gallon from the average of $3.70.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        [69]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On August 8, oil fell over 6 percent, in its largest drop since May, to $81, its lowest price of the year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On September 24, oil reached $79.85, down 9 percent for the week, due to concerns about another recession and the overall world economy. The average price of gas was $3.51, with predictions of $3.25 by November, but it was below $3 in some markets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        [71]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During October, the price of oil rose 22 percent, the fastest pace since February, as worries over the U.S. economy decreased, leading to predictions of $4 by early 2012. As of November 8, the price reached $96.80. Gas prices were not following the increase, due to lower demand resulting from the economy, the normal decrease in travel, lower oil prices in other countries, and production of winter blends which cost less. The average rose slightly to $3.41 but predictions of $3.25 were made.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        [72]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2012">
       2012
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2012">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brent_versus_WTI.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2480" data-file-width="3508" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Brent_versus_WTI.png/220px-Brent_versus_WTI.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Brent_versus_WTI.png/330px-Brent_versus_WTI.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Brent_versus_WTI.png/440px-Brent_versus_WTI.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brent_versus_WTI.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Brent versus WTI
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Shortages of oil could have resulted if
      <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
       Iran
      </a>
      closed the
      <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">
       Strait of Hormuz
      </a>
      , through which one-fifth of exported oil travels, as a result of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Union_sanctions_against_Iran" title="European Union sanctions against Iran">
       sanctions
      </a>
      due to the country's
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran" title="Nuclear program of Iran">
       nuclear policies
      </a>
      . The price of oil stayed near $100 throughout January because of concerns over supplies, and the European debt situation. The average price of gas was $3.38 on January 20, up 17 cents from a month earlier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        [73]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another factor was planned closing of refineries in the U.S. and Europe due to lower demand.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By early February, the national average was $3.48, though oil prices were at $98, the lowest in six weeks, and U.S. demand was the lowest since September 2001.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        [76]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On February 20, benchmark March crude oil reached $105.21, the highest in nine months. This came one day after Iran's oil ministry announced an end to sales to British and French companies; though this would have little actual impact on supplies, fears resulted in higher prices. Also, approval of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_government_debt_crisis#Fifth_austerity_package_.E2.80.93_February_2012" title="Greek government debt crisis">
       bailout plan for Greece
      </a>
      was expected, and China's action to raise the money supply was likely to stimulate the economy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Brent crude was up 11 percent for the year to $119.58 on February 17, with cold weather in Europe and higher
      <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">
       Third World
      </a>
      demand, and
      <a href="/wiki/West_Texas_Intermediate" title="West Texas Intermediate">
       West Texas Intermediate
      </a>
      crude was up 19 percent to $103.24. The average price of gas was $3.53.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        [78]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On February 29, the average was $3.73.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The average peaked at $3.94 early in April,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and on April 24, it was $3.85 compared to $3.86 a year earlier; it had been two years since gas prices were lower than the previous year. Crude oil prices were down; West Texas Intermediate was $103.55 a barrel,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kahn_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kahn-84">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
      down from over $107 late in March,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        [85]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Brent Crude $118.16
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kahn_84-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kahn-84">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
      after peaking above $128 in March.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        [86]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On May 7, benchmark U.S. crude reached $95.34, the lowest price of the year, after voters in
      <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
       France
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
       Greece
      </a>
      ousted government officials who would cut spending to solve the debt crisis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        [87]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Benchmark oil in New York actually rose for two days straight early in June, to $84.29. With U.S. oil supplies the highest since 1990, gas reached $3.57 on June 5.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After falling again to its lowest price since October 2011, Benchmark crude rose 5.8 percent to $82.18 on June 29, with Brent crude up 4.5 percent to $95.51. European bailout efforts included
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis#Direct_loans_to_banks_and_banking_regulation" title="European sovereign-debt crisis">
       lending money to banks
      </a>
      , decreasing likelihood of failures. Also, European countries decided not to buy Iranian oil. The price of gas was $3.35, the lowest since January 6.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        [89]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 17, Benchmark Crude reached $89.22 and Brent crude $104 after good economic news in the United States. Gas rose to $3.40.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        [90]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On August 7, a California refinery fire contributed to a jump in oil futures. Other refinery problems, a pipeline leak, fears about Iran,
      <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">
       the crisis in Syria
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">
       North Sea
      </a>
      problems, and
      <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ernesto_(2012)" title="Hurricane Ernesto (2012)">
       Tropical Storm Ernesto
      </a>
      all contributed to a 20 percent jump in oil prices in six weeks. The price of gas reached $3.63 but was not expected to go much higher.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        [91]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Good economic news in the United States contributed to oil reaching its highest price since May on August 17, with Benchmark Crude reaching $96.01, while Brent crude fell slightly to $113.71.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Early in September, a mix of bad economic news from the United States and good economic news from Europe caused the price of oil to fall slightly. On September 4, Benchmark Crude reached $95.41, with Brent crude at $114.84. The price of gas went down slightly to $3.82
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        [93]
       </a>
      </sup>
      but was still the highest ever for
      <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">
       Labor Day
      </a>
      weekend.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isaac_(2012)" title="Hurricane Isaac (2012)">
       Hurricane Isaac
      </a>
      contributed to a temporary spike in gas prices, but on September 12 gas once again rose, to $3.86, as refineries cut production prior to the switch from summer blend gasoline to winter blend. Benchmark Crude also reached its highest level since early May and continued to rise above $99 after
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve" title="Federal Reserve">
       Federal Reserve
      </a>
      announcements of actions to improve the economy and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_diplomatic_missions_attacks" title="2012 diplomatic missions attacks">
       2012 diplomatic missions attacks
      </a>
      . Brent crude rose slightly to nearly $116.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        [95]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        [96]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Early in October, the average gas price was $3.78 and falling, though still a record for the month.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        [98]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Late in the month, the average reached $3.62 after a 13-cent drop in a week, the most since November 2008. Brent crude was down $8 in the previous month.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        [99]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the start of November, the average was $3.54, partly due to lower demand after
      <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">
       Hurricane Sandy
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        [100]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Crude oil futures fell after
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      was re-elected November 6.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        [101]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After
      <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving" title="Thanksgiving">
       Thanksgiving
      </a>
      , lower U.S. oil inventories, good economic news in the United States and good news relating to the Greek bailout helped push Brent crude up to $111.04, and benchmark oil for January delivery to $87.92; benchmark oil reached $86.24 on November 28, and gas was $3.41.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        [103]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 13, Brent crude was down to $109.20, while benchmark oil fell slightly due to
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_fiscal_cliff" title="United States fiscal cliff">
       U.S. fiscal cliff
      </a>
      concerns and rose due to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve" title="Federal Reserve">
       Federal Reserve
      </a>
      efforts to help the U.S. economy, ending the day at $86.77.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        [104]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In mid-December, gas prices reached $3.25, the lowest for 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        [105]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Oil was trading for between $84 and $90.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        [106]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2013">
       2013
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2013">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      On January 17, with good economic news in the United States, Benchmark oil reached its highest level since September, going over $95. Brent crude rose above $110. Gas was at $3.29.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan_107-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jan-107">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Refinery shutdowns led to a dramatic rise in gas prices. Late in February, gas was at $3.78, up 14 cents from a week earlier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        [109]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On February 25, with European stock markets doing well, Benchmark crude for April rose above $94 after a significant drop the previous week due to news the Federal Reserve might end its stimulus efforts, making the dollar stronger. Brent crude was over $115.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two days later gas reached its highest point, $3.79 a gallon. By mid-April, with low demand expected due to negative economic news, gas was down to $3.56 as Brent crude fell to $103.04, its lowest price since July.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With economic problems worldwide leading to low demand, gas prices fell 3 percent in April, the most in a month in ten years, to the lowest level for that month since 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        [112]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Before
      <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Day" title="Memorial Day">
       Memorial Day
      </a>
      , when gas was $3.63,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahey_113-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fahey-113">
        [113]
       </a>
      </sup>
      gas supplies fell even though oil supplies were the highest in 35 years. U.S. economic news was also negative. On May 30, Benchmark crude for July rose slightly to $93.61 after falling the previous day, and Brent crude fell slightly to $102.19.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On June 5 the price of oil rose again with supplies lower. Benchmark crude rose above $94. The price of gas was $3.62.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On June 12, the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">
       International Energy Agency
      </a>
      said demand for oil would still rise in 2013, but not as much as previously believed due to the economy. Also, May OPEC production was the highest in seven months. Benchmark crude fell slightly to $95.31, and Brent crude rose to $103.27.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On June 20, with the Federal Reserve stating that its stimulus program could end if the U.S. economy continued to improve, as well as economic problems in China, Benchmark crude fell below $97. Brent crude fell to $104.24.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 10, oil prices were the highest in more than a year as a result of lower supplies and
      <a href="/wiki/2013_Egyptian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2013 Egyptian coup d'état">
       trouble in Egypt
      </a>
      . In the past week, Brent crude had climbed 7 percent to $108.51. Because too much oil was being produced for the infrastructure to handle it, West Texas Intermediate was lower than Brent crude for several years; it has returned to being consistent with Brent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 5 it reached $103.22.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 19 with good economic news in the United States, Benchmark crude reached $108.05, while gas was $3.67, the highest on a Friday since March 22. Brent crude was at $108.07.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $3.63 on August 1, though good economic news in the U.S., China and Europe meant oil was going up again after a decline the previous week. Benchmark crude reached $107.89, while Brent crude was $109.54.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On August 16 Benchmark oil was $107.46 after six days of increases as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_violence_in_Egypt_(July_2013%E2%80%93present)" title="Political violence in Egypt (July 2013–present)">
       Egypt's problems continued
      </a>
      . The concern was access to the
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
       Suez Canal
      </a>
      , which appears unlikely to be a problem but still concerns companies. Brent crude was $110.48 on August 19.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On August 28 West Texas intermediate reached $110.10, the highest since May 2011, and Brent crude reached $116.61, its highest point since February 19, due to concern about U.S. involvement in
      <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">
       Syria
      </a>
      . Meanwhile, inventories in the United States had their biggest increase in four months.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Benchmark crude rose to $107.56 on September 11 due to lower supplies after dropping due to hopes for a peaceful Syria solution; Brent crude rose to $111.50.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        [125]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Gas was $3.59 at the start of the month, but at the end of September, the price of gas was $3.39, the lowest for the time of year since 2010. The New York Mercantile Exchange price on September 27 was $102.87. Refineries had no hurricanes or other problems.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        [126]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        [127]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Benchmark crude fell to $103.31 on October 3 after the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_federal_government_shutdown_of_2013" title="United States federal government shutdown of 2013">
       U.S. government shutdown
      </a>
      , and Brent crude was $109.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On October 21, Benchmark crude was $99.22, the first time below $100 since July. Higher supplies and fewer threats from the Middle East were the reasons. Brent crude was $109.64 and gas reached $3.35.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        [129]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On November 13, Brent crude reached $107.12 and was $13.24 higher than West Texas Intermediate, the largest difference since April, due to trouble in Libya and sanctions against Iran.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        [130]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On November 25, Benchmark crude decreased to $93.92 while Brent crude reached $110.41 after the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geneva_interim_agreement_on_Iranian_nuclear_program" title="Geneva interim agreement on Iranian nuclear program">
       agreement regarding Iran's nuclear program
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        [131]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On December 16, Benchmark crude rose to $97.44 and Brent crude reached $110.53 with good economic news from Europe and more Libya trouble. Gas was $3.23, three cents higher than a month earlier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        [132]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On December 27, due to a better economy in the United States leading to higher demand, oil closed about $100 for the first time since October. Gas was $3.27, two cents below a year earlier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gorondi_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gorondi-133">
        [133]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2014">
       2014
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2014">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      On January 2, Benchmark crude fell by the most in one day since November 2012 to close at $95.44. Brent crude was $107.78. Gas was $3.33.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gorondi_133-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gorondi-133">
        [133]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geneva_interim_agreement_on_Iranian_nuclear_program" title="Geneva interim agreement on Iranian nuclear program">
       Iran agreement
      </a>
      and increased production from
      <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
       Libya
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">
       North Sea
      </a>
      , Benchmark oil was around $92 on January 13 and Brent crude was $105.98.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After good economic news from
      <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
       Japan
      </a>
      , Benchmark crude fell slightly from its highest close of 2014, $98.23 on January 30. Brent crude fell to $107.25. The difference between the two fell below $10 for the first time since November, partly due to cold weather in the United States which resulted in high heating oil demand.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        [135]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Early in February gas was $3.27.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dallas_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dallas-136">
        [136]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cold weather led to the price of oil staying above $100 for most of February, but lower prices were expected. With United States fourth quarter economic growth expected to be lower than an early estimate, Benchmark crude fell slightly on February 27 to $102.40, with Brent crude reaching $108.61.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        [137]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On March 24, due to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accession_of_Crimea_to_the_Russian_Federation" title="Accession of Crimea to the Russian Federation">
       the dispute over Crimea
      </a>
      , problems in Libya, and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_oil_spills#Complete" title="List of oil spills">
       the Houston Ship Channel collision
      </a>
      , Benchmark crude rose above $100 and Brent crude rose to $107.41. Economic problems in China kept prices from going even higher.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        [138]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Later in the week, good economic news from the United States, lower oil supplies in Oklahoma and a
      <a href="/wiki/Shell_Nigeria#Recent_news" title="Shell Nigeria">
       force majeure by Shell Nigeria
      </a>
      pushed prices slightly higher, to $102.12 for Benchmark crude and $108.29 for Brent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        [139]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On April 7, Benchmark crude fell below $101 and Brent crude fell to $105.64 with news that Libya might open more terminals in May,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        [140]
       </a>
      </sup>
      but more
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine" title="2014 Russian military intervention in Ukraine">
       Ukraine problems
      </a>
      pushed the prices back up on April 8.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        [141]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $3.59, matching the level in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dallas_136-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dallas-136">
        [136]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Continued Ukraine problems pushed oil higher on April 24, with Benchmark crude at $101.94 and Brent crude at $110.33, though an April 23 report said U.S. oil supplies were higher than expected. The price of gas was $3.68.5, the highest since March 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        [142]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On April 30, Benchmark crude dropped below $100 for the first time in three weeks as oil supplies continued to rise and the unusually cold winter resulted in negative U.S. economic news. Gas was up 14 cents for the month, the most in three years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        [143]
       </a>
      </sup>
      More Ukraine trouble pushed Benchmark crude above $100 and Brent crude over $108 on May 12,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        [144]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and further problems in Libya helped push Benchmark crude over $102 and Brent crude over $110 by May 15, though negative economic news in the U.S. and an unexpected increase in oil stockpiles pushed Benchmark crude back down temporarily.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        [145]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        [146]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Continued concerns over Ukraine and Libya pushed oil back above $104.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        [147]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The price of gas was $3.65.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahey_113-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fahey-113">
        [113]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Iraq_offensive_(June_2014)" title="Northern Iraq offensive (June 2014)">
       Trouble in Iraq
      </a>
      resulted in higher prices for oil and gas in June. West Texas crude reached $106 and Brent crude $115.75. At the end of the month Benchmark crude was just above $105 while Brent crude fell below $113.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strauss_148-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Strauss-148">
        [148]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
       <a href="#cite_note-149">
        [149]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The price of gas was $3.66.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
       <a href="#cite_note-150">
        [150]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After three weeks of going down, U.S. crude fell below $100 for the first time since May on July 15. However, with
      <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">
       Middle East
      </a>
      and Ukraine problems sending oil higher, Benchmark crude finished July 18 just above $103, with Brent crude staying above $107.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        [151]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With low demand and plentiful supplies, and despite good economic news from China and the United States, Brent crude fell below $107 on July 24, and U.S. crude dropped to $102.10.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
       <a href="#cite_note-152">
        [152]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 28, gas was $3.52, down five cents from a week earlier, due to refiners cutting prices.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        [153]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two weeks later gas was $3.48, less than a year earlier.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
       <a href="#cite_note-154">
        [154]
       </a>
      </sup>
      And on August 14, light sweet oil was $95.58, the lowest since January, while Brent crude reached $102.01, the lowest since June, after falling the most in one day since January. Production in Libya was up, and economic slowdowns were expected in Europe and China, making even lower prices likely.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        [155]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of Labor Day, gas was $3.41, 18 cents lower than in 2013. Low demand and high North American production cancelled out effects of troubles in the Middle East and Ukraine. West Texas crude was below $94 on August 27 and Brent crude below $103.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Strauss_148-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Strauss-148">
        [148]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On October 16, West Texas crude fell below $80 for the first time in more than two years, while Brent crude reached $82.60, the lowest since November 2010. OPEC Members were not expected to act as increases in the U.S. supply resulting from high
      <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">
       oil shale
      </a>
      production added to a worldwide surplus.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        [156]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On October 31, the average price of gas reached $3 and was expected to go below that figure for the first time since December 2010. Demand for oil was down and there were many new sources. United States oil production was up 70 percent since 2008, and Iraq and Canada were producing more.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
       <a href="#cite_note-157">
        [157]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the Lundberg survey released December 7, gas was down 12 cents from two weeks earlier to $2.72. Demand was low while production was high, and the strong dollar contributed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        [158]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With demand low in China and Europe and OPEC deciding not to cut back, West Texas Intermediate reached $63.50 on December 8, the lowest since July 2009, while Brent crude reached $66.90, a level not seen since October 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        [159]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After
      <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
       Saudi Arabia
      </a>
      oil minister
      <a href="/wiki/Ali_Al-Naimi" title="Ali Al-Naimi">
       Ali Al-Naimi
      </a>
      said OPEC members could not cut production on their own,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
       <a href="#cite_note-160">
        [160]
       </a>
      </sup>
      oil prices rose slightly December 18 but finished the day lower with Benchmark crude at $54.11 and Brent crude $59.27, both the lowest since May 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        [161]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.49 a gallon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
       <a href="#cite_note-162">
        [162]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Days later gas was $2.38, the lowest in five years, after 89 straight days of going down, the longest continuous decline ever according to
      <a href="/wiki/American_Automobile_Association" title="American Automobile Association">
       AAA
      </a>
      . The price of oil was down 50 percent since April, while gas had fallen 36 percent. Economic problems in Europe and Asia, high gas mileage, a strong dollar, higher U.S. production and no action by OPEC have been credited.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        [163]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      By 12 December 2014, the price of benchmark crude oil, both Brent and WTI reached their lowest prices since 2009. Brent crude oil and accordingly to all type of Crude Oil dropped to US$62.75 a barrel for January delivery on the London-based
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICE_Futures_Europe" title="ICE Futures Europe">
       ICE Futures Europe
      </a>
      exchange and futures for West Texas Intermediate (WTI) for January settlement slid to $58.80 a barrel in electronic trading on the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mercantile_Exchange" title="New York Mercantile Exchange">
       New York Mercantile Exchange
      </a>
      (NYME). This represents a 40 percent decrease in 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Financial_POst2014_164-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Financial_POst2014-164">
        [164]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The CIBC reported that the global oil industry continued to produce massive amounts of oil in spite of a stagnant crude oil market. Oil production from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakken_formation" title="Bakken formation">
       Bakken formation
      </a>
      was forecast in 2012 to grow by 600,000 barrels every year through 2016. By 2012 Canadian tight oil and oil sands production was also surging.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-albertaoil2012_165-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-albertaoil2012-165">
        [165]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 2014 crude oil prices dropped by about a third as U.S. shale oil production increased and China and Europe's demand for oil decreased. In spite of huge global oversupply, on 27 November 2014 in Vienna, Saudi Oil Minister Ali al-Naimi blocked the appeals from the poorer OPEC member states, such as Venezuela, Iran and Algeria, for production cuts. The European crude oil benchmark, Brent, plunged to US$71.25, a four-year low. Al-Naimi argued that the market would be left to correct itself, this will put pressure on companies in the US to reduce shale fracturing operations. OPEC had a "long-standing policy of defending prices". OPEC is ready to let the Brent oil price drop to $60 to slow down US shale oil production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        [166]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In spite of a troubled economy in member countries, al-Naimi repeated his statement on Saudi inaction on 10 December 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krishnan2014_167-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Krishnan2014-167">
        [167]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the end of 2014, as the demand for global oil consumption continued to decline, the remarkably rapid oil output growth in ‘light, tight’ oil production in the North Dakota
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakken_formation" title="Bakken formation">
       Bakken
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Permian_basin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Permian basin (page does not exist)">
       Permian
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eagle_Ford_Formation" title="Eagle Ford Formation">
       Eagle Ford
      </a>
      Basins in Texas, while rejuvenating economic growth in "U.S. refining, petrochemical and associated transportation industries, rail &amp; pipelines, destabilized international oil markets."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mohr_2014_168-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mohr_2014-168">
        [168]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2015">
       2015
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2015">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      On January 16, Brent crude rose as high as $50.16 before falling back, and the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">
       International Energy Agency
      </a>
      said production was down due to lower prices and higher prices were likely late in 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        [169]
       </a>
      </sup>
      West Texas Intermediate, down 10 percent for the month, closed at $48.48 on January 14
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        [170]
       </a>
      </sup>
      after closing at $45.89 the previous day. Gas was $2.12.
