      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        [171]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After the January 23 death of
      <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Abdullah of Saudi Arabia">
       King Abdullah
      </a>
      led to concerns about the future, West Texas Intermediate climbed as high as $47.76 and Brent crude reached $49.80.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        [172]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From January 30 to February 3, oil rose 20 percent, but on February 4, U.S. crude futures fell 8.7 percent to $48.45, the most in one day since November 28, 2014. Brent crude fell from $59 to $54 two weeks after reaching $45. U.S. inventories were the highest since 1982, while the dollar was recovering from "its worst day in more than a year."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        [173]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Although inventory remained high, Brent crude reached its highest price of 2015 on February 17, closing at $62.53 after reaching $63. Problems in the Middle East, especially Libya, contributed to the rise. Fighting in Ukraine was also a factor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        [174]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At the end of February, with refineries changing to summer blend, the price of gas was $2.37,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tracy_175-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tracy-175">
        [175]
       </a>
      </sup>
      up from $2.03 in January.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahey_March_2015_176-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fahey_March_2015-176">
        [176]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other factors included an explosion at a
      <a href="/wiki/Torrance,_California" title="Torrance, California">
       Torrance, California
      </a>
      refinery and a
      <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">
       strike
      </a>
      involving steel workers at 20 refineries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tracy_175-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tracy-175">
        [175]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On March 13, oil declined 5 percent for a total drop of 10 percent for the week.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahey_March_2015_176-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fahey_March_2015-176">
        [176]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Benchmark crude reached $45.16
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
       <a href="#cite_note-177">
        [177]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Brent crude was $56.24.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
       <a href="#cite_note-178">
        [178]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Supplies continued to increase and the price was expected to fall until changes by refineries for summer. Gas reached $2.46 March 7 but fell to $2.44 a week later.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahey_March_2015_176-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fahey_March_2015-176">
        [176]
       </a>
      </sup>
      U.S. inventories were the highest since records had been kept, but on March 18, with the Federal Reserve indicating interest rates would not rise quickly, oil prices increased 6 percent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
       <a href="#cite_note-179">
        [179]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Brent crude rose 16 percent in April, reaching $64.95, its highest price for 2015, on April 16. U.S. crude was $56.62 on April 17. Reasons were a drop in expected
      <a href="/wiki/Shale_oil" title="Shale oil">
       shale oil
      </a>
      production in the United States and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yemeni_Civil_War_(2015)" title="Yemeni Civil War (2015)">
       war in Yemen
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
       <a href="#cite_note-180">
        [180]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.41, up a penny in a week.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
       <a href="#cite_note-181">
        [181]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On May 5, gas reached $2.63 after rising for 19 days; gas was going up faster than oil,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
       <a href="#cite_note-182">
        [182]
       </a>
      </sup>
      which reached its highest 2015 price, $61.10 for U.S. crude and $68.40 for Brent crude, before settling at $60.40 and $67.52 respectively. The dollar was lower but different sources conflicted over whether U.S. inventories were down for the first time in 2015, or up as they had been.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
       <a href="#cite_note-183">
        [183]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      West Texas Intermediate closed slightly higher at $58.98 on May 19, and Brent crude rose slightly to just over $65 as U.S. supplies, still near records, fell while refineries increased production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
       <a href="#cite_note-184">
        [184]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On May 26, gas was $2.74.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
       <a href="#cite_note-185">
        [185]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 10, West Texas Intermediate reached $61.43, the highest price since December. Demand was expected to stay high, but OPEC production was also staying high. Brent crude was $65.70
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
       <a href="#cite_note-186">
        [186]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
       <a href="#cite_note-187">
        [187]
       </a>
      </sup>
      while gas was $2.76.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
       <a href="#cite_note-188">
        [188]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 1, with an increase in U.S. inventory for the first time in two months, U.S. benchmark oil fell by the most in one day since April 8 to $56.26, the lowest since April 22, while Brent crude fell to $62.01.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
       <a href="#cite_note-189">
        [189]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.77.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
       <a href="#cite_note-190">
        [190]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Oil fell by about $10 in July as the U.S. dollar was strong, supplies were high, and the Chinese stock market was down. Near the end of the month, Brent crude reached $53.31, close to the lowest in six months, while U.S. crude, at $48.52, was close to a four-month low,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
       <a href="#cite_note-191">
        [191]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and gas was $2.69.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
       <a href="#cite_note-192">
        [192]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A week later, with supplies high and summer driving in the United States ending, oil fell below $45, close to the six-year low reached in March.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
       <a href="#cite_note-193">
        [193]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Brent crude was below $50.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
       <a href="#cite_note-194">
        [194]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.64.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
       <a href="#cite_note-195">
        [195]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On August 11, U.S. crude reached $43.08, its lowest price since February 2009. Brent crude was below $50.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
       <a href="#cite_note-196">
        [196]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.59.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
       <a href="#cite_note-197">
        [197]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On August 26, U.S. crude reached $38.60,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
       <a href="#cite_note-198">
        [198]
       </a>
      </sup>
      once again its lowest price since February 2009, before jumping more than 10 percent the next day to $42.56 for its biggest increase in one day since March 2009. Brent crude was up 10 percent to $47. U.S. supplies had fallen dramatically, especially in
      <a href="/wiki/Cushing,_Oklahoma" title="Cushing, Oklahoma">
       Cushing, Oklahoma
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
       <a href="#cite_note-199">
        [199]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.56, the lowest at this time of year since 2004, though refinery problems kept it from being lower.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
       <a href="#cite_note-200">
        [200]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During August, Brent reached a low of $42.23 and U.S. crude was as low as $37.75.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNBC2015_201-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNBC2015-201">
        [201]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Then U.S. crude jumped 28 percent in 3 days, the most since 1990. Brent crude also climbed 28 percent above $54, the highest in a month.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
       <a href="#cite_note-202">
        [202]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On September 11,
      <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">
       Goldman Sachs
      </a>
      predicted continued surpluses and falling prices, and U.S. crude fell to $44.74 while Brent crude reached $47.93.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
       <a href="#cite_note-203">
        [203]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.37.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
       <a href="#cite_note-204">
        [204]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A drop in supplies from Cushing, speculation about Federal Reserve action on interest rates, and U.S. help for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurd" title="Kurd">
       Kurds
      </a>
      in Syria contributed to a rise in U.S. crude to $47.15, while Brent was $50.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNBC2015_201-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNBC2015-201">
        [201]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On September 25, the price of gas was $2.29.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
       <a href="#cite_note-205">
        [205]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On September 29, with U.S. crude inventories up and Cushing supplies falling more slowly, West Texas Intermediate finished at $45.23, with Brent crude falling to $47.97.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
       <a href="#cite_note-206">
        [206]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After an International Energy Agency prediction of high supplies for the next year, U.S. crude fell the most in a week in more than two months, ending October 15 below $47, and Brent crude had its biggest loss for a week in nearly two months, just under $50 on October 16.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
       <a href="#cite_note-207">
        [207]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With Middle Eastern countries producing more oil than needed and Iran expected to add even more as a result of the
      <a href="/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action" title="Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action">
       nuclear deal
      </a>
      , as well as slow growth in China, U.S. crude fell below $46 on October 19 and Brent crude reached $48,51 early October 20.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
       <a href="#cite_note-208">
        [208]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.25.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209">
       <a href="#cite_note-209">
        [209]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On November 4, prices fell over 3 percent as a result of higher U.S. inventories and U.S. output, before rising slightly, Brent crude recovering to $48.76 and West Texas Intermediate reaching $46.37.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
       <a href="#cite_note-210">
        [210]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.19, the lowest for the time of year since 2004.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
       <a href="#cite_note-211">
        [211]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On November 19, U.S. crude fell below $40, and Brent crude slipped below $44.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
       <a href="#cite_note-212">
        [212]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.13.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
       <a href="#cite_note-213">
        [213]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Higher demand, winter weather in the United States and a promise by
      <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
       Saudi Arabia
      </a>
      to work toward stabilizing prices sent West Texas Intermediate back over $42 and Brent crude over $44 on November 23.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
       <a href="#cite_note-214">
        [214]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On the first week of December Brent crude fell to $42.43 and U.S. crude slipped below $40 after OPEC first said it would increase production and then decided not to make changes. Other factors were a weak dollar and a strong Euro.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
       <a href="#cite_note-215">
        [215]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 11, oil fell to $35.62. The next day, gas was $2.02, the lowest in over six years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
       <a href="#cite_note-216">
        [216]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 21, Brent crude fell as low as $36.35 a barrel; this was the lowest price since July 2004.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217">
       <a href="#cite_note-217">
        [217]
       </a>
      </sup>
      U.S. crude rose slightly to $36.14.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218">
       <a href="#cite_note-218">
        [218]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas fell below $2 for the first time since 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
       <a href="#cite_note-219">
        [219]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 30 with U.S. supplies still high, light sweet crude fell to $36.60, while Brent crude reached $36.46. Oil ended the year down 30 percent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
       <a href="#cite_note-220">
        [220]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In early 2015, the US oil price fell below $50 per barrel dragging Brent oil to just below $50 as well.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_below_50_221-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC_below_50-221">
        [221]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Steve Briese, a commodity analyst, who had forecasted in March 2014 a decline to world price to $75 from $100, based on 30 years of extra supply
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222">
       <a href="#cite_note-222">
        [222]
       </a>
      </sup>
      in early December 2014 projected a low of $35 a barrel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
       <a href="#cite_note-223">
        [223]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On Jan 8, 2015 commodity hedge fund manager Andrew J. Hall suggested that $40-a-barrel is close to “an absolute price floor,” adding that a significant amount of U.S. and Canadian production can’t cover the cash costs of operating at that price.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224">
       <a href="#cite_note-224">
        [224]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In mid-January 2015, Goldman Sachs predicted the U.S. oil benchmark to average $40.50 a barrel and Brent to average $42 a barrel in the second quarter. For the year, Goldman sees Brent prices averaging $50.40 and for the U.S. benchmark, $47.15 a barrel in 2015, down from $73.75.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225">
       <a href="#cite_note-225">
        [225]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Business" title="Bloomberg Business">
       Bloomberg Business
      </a>
      , the efficiency of
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_2015_March_226-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_2015_March-226">
        [226]
       </a>
      </sup>
      newer shale oil wells that use
      <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_fracturing" title="Hydraulic fracturing">
       hydraulic fracturing
      </a>
      in the United States, combined with the US$12 million upfront well drilling and construction costs, provide incentives to oil producers to continue to flood the already glutted market with under-priced oil in spite of crude oil storage limitations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_2015_March_226-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_2015_March-226">
        [226]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many less efficient and less productive older wells were shut down but these shale oil wells continue to increase production while making a profit in a market where crude oil is priced as low as US$50 a barrel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_2015_March_226-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_2015_March-226">
        [226]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 16 April the price of WTI hit a high of $56.52 for 2015 following the publication of the monthly review by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Petroleum_Exporting_Countries" title="Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries">
       Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries
      </a>
      in which it was reported that oil production in the United States had peaked and would start to decline in the third quarter thereby easing the global glut of crude.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_2015_227-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WSJ_2015-227">
        [227]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From 6–7 December the price of WTI crude fell about five percent, closing under $40 for the second time in the year, due to OPEC refusing to scale back production. This met with negative reactions in the stock market, causing the DJIA and the S&amp;P 500 procuring a net negative run for 2015.
     </p>
     <p>
      In late 2015, an Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries (OPEC) member Venezuela's Oil Minister Eulogio del Pino and a Goldman Sachs analyst Michele Della Vigna suggested that oil may go as low as $20-per-barrel mark, although with a 15% probability, and that it would only be temporary.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
       <a href="#cite_note-228">
        [228]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
       <a href="#cite_note-229">
        [229]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Lord Browne, the former chief executive of BP, did not rule out the possibility when asked asked if oil could hit $20 a barrel. He added: “In the long run, $20 is probably wrong, but that’s as far as I’d go.”
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230">
       <a href="#cite_note-230">
        [230]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 11, the price of WTI crude hit a seven-year low, settling around $35 for the day. Once again various stocks slid as this unfolded, erasing the previous day's rally.
     </p>
     <p>
      On December 21, the price of WTI crude hit an eleven-year low, as it dropped below $34 a barrel for the first time since 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231">
       <a href="#cite_note-231">
        [231]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2016">
       2016
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2016">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      On January 6, 2016, the price of WTI crude hit another eleven-year low, as it dropped to 32.53 a barrel for the first time since 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
       <a href="#cite_note-232">
        [232]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On January 12, in its seventh losing day, crude oil dropped below $30 for the first time since December 2003, ending the day at $30.44, as gas fell below $1.97.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
       <a href="#cite_note-233">
        [233]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Brent crude hit $27.10 on January 20, the lowest since November 2003.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rise_234-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rise-234">
        [234]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Oil rose again before falling January 25, Brent crude reaching $30.86 and U.S. oil $30.68.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
       <a href="#cite_note-235">
        [235]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After OPEC encouraged production cuts and U.S. GDP data suggested fewer interest rate increases, U.S. oil had four days of gains to finish January at $33.62. Brent was $34.74.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rise_234-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rise-234">
        [234]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $1.81, the lowest since January 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
       <a href="#cite_note-236">
        [236]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A February 7 meeting between
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ali_al-Naimi" title="Ali al-Naimi">
       Ali al-Naimi
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">
       Saudi Arabia
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Eulogio_Del_Pino&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Eulogio Del Pino (page does not exist)">
       Eulogio Del Pino
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
       Venezuela
      </a>
      failed to produce desired results, and oil fell the next day, with Brent crude at $33.53 by noon and U.S. crude at $30.27.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
       <a href="#cite_note-237">
        [237]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On February 11, U.S. crude reached $26.21 after reaching $26.05, its lowest price since May 2003. The next day oil rose 12.3 percent to $29.44, the most in one day since February 2009. Investors wanted to be ready when the price started going up. Also, OPEC was "ready to cooperate" on lower production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238">
       <a href="#cite_note-238">
        [238]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239">
       <a href="#cite_note-239">
        [239]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On February 22, Benchmark U.S. crude rose 6.2 percent to $31.48 and Brent crude went up 5.1 percent to $34.69 after news that supplies were expected to grow more slowly.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
       <a href="#cite_note-240">
        [240]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the end of the week, West Texas Intermediate was up 3 percent to $32.78, and Brent was up 7 percent to $35.12 after rising as high as $37, the most since January 5. Pipeline outages in Nigeria and Iraq, a lower number of active U.S. rigs, and lower gasoline inventories for the first time since November were reasons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
       <a href="#cite_note-241">
        [241]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $1.73, down 10 cents from the previous month, but with the switch to summer blend in California, gas was $2.34 and on its way back up.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242">
       <a href="#cite_note-242">
        [242]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After inventories fell faster than expected, U.S. crude was $37.94 on March 9, while Brent crude was up again to $40.84 after six straight up days and its highest level in three months the previous day then a 3 percent drop due to concerns about too much oil. Prices were up 25 percent after major oil producers said they would keep supplies at January levels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243">
       <a href="#cite_note-243">
        [243]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After reducing the number of rigs for 12 weeks, U.S. producers added one rig with oil up 50 percent. With gasoline demand up, Brent crude reached its highest level of the year at $42.54 before falling to $41.20 March 18 in its fourth straight week of gains. U.S. crude also reached a high at $41.20 before falling to $39.44, ending its fifth straight week higher.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244">
       <a href="#cite_note-244">
        [244]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.02, up 17 cents in 2 weeks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245">
       <a href="#cite_note-245">
        [245]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On March 31, U.S. crude reached $37.57, the lowest since March 31, as the country's supply hit a record for the seventh week. Brent crude was $38.81.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246">
       <a href="#cite_note-246">
        [246]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the first week of April with a weak dollar, oil jumped 7 percent, with Benchmark crude reaching $39.72 and Brent at $41.94.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247">
       <a href="#cite_note-247">
        [247]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The next Tuesday, Brent hit $43.58, the highest of the year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248">
       <a href="#cite_note-248">
        [248]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      With a planned meeting of oil producers to discuss keeping output where it was, on April 15 oil fell over 3 percent, with U.S. crude reaching $40.33 by midday and Brent at $42.82.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249">
       <a href="#cite_note-249">
        [249]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      With high demand in the U.S., lower production worldwide and problems in oil fields, oil rose for the third straight week, with Brent crude rising 4.5 percent for the week to $45.11 and West Texas Intermediate up more than 8 percent at $43.73.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250">
       <a href="#cite_note-250">
        [250]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On April 26, U.S. inventories were down after analysts had expected a supply increase, and the dollar was weak. U.S. crude was up 3 percent to $44.04 while Brent crude was up to $45.74.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251">
       <a href="#cite_note-251">
        [251]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/2016_Fort_McMurray_wildfire" title="2016 Fort McMurray wildfire">
       The fire
      </a>
      in Canada, attacks in
      <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
       Nigeria
      </a>
      , and economic problems and the
      <a href="/wiki/Zika_virus" title="Zika virus">
       Zika virus
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
       Venezuela
      </a>
      led to supply problems and the highest prices in seven months on May 16.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252">
       <a href="#cite_note-252">
        [252]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With U.S. supplies down more than predicted, West Texas intermediate reached $49.56 on May 25, the highest since October. Brent crude was $49.74.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253">
       <a href="#cite_note-253">
        [253]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On June 7, with the dollar lower and interest rates not expected to rise after U.S. economic news, Benchmark crude closed over $50 for the first time since July 21. Brent crude was $51.44.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254">
       <a href="#cite_note-254">
        [254]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      With the June 23
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      vote
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">
       to leave
      </a>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      , U.S. oil fell $2.05 to $48.06 and Brent crude fell $2.13 to $48.78.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255">
       <a href="#cite_note-255">
        [255]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Gas was $2.29 on June 30, the lowest for the
      <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">
       July 4
      </a>
      holiday in 13 years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256">
       <a href="#cite_note-256">
        [256]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 7, although supplies were down, they were not as low as forecast, and U.S. crude reached $47.20, down 4.7 percent. Brent crude reached $46.27, the lowest since May 11.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257">
       <a href="#cite_note-257">
        [257]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For the week ending July 15, crude supplies fell, but gasoline supplies rose. After gains on July 20, West Texas Intermediate fell to $44.75 and Brent crude went down to $46.20.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258">
       <a href="#cite_note-258">
        [258]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.19, the lowest since 2004 at that time of year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259">
       <a href="#cite_note-259">
        [259]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On August 5, West Texas Intermediate fell to $41.52 as the dollar rose as a result of better U.S. job news than expected, while Brent crude fell to $43.95. Oil prices had fallen more than 20 percent since June and were rising earlier in the week.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260">
       <a href="#cite_note-260">
        [260]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On the week ending August 12, Benchmark crude rose 6.4 percent, and it went over $45 on August 15. Brent crude was $47.59.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261">
       <a href="#cite_note-261">
        [261]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gas was $2.12.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262">
       <a href="#cite_note-262">
        [262]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On August 31, U.S. government data showed a higher than expected increase in oil supplies, and the prediction that supplies would stay high. If the Fed raised interest rates, a higher dollar and lower oil prices would result. U.S. crude fell to $43.16 on September 1, its lowest level in 3 weeks. Brent reached $45.52. Oil had gone up 11 percent for the month with the expectation that OPEC would limit production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263">
       <a href="#cite_note-263">
        [263]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Pipeline" title="Colonial Pipeline">
       Colonial Pipeline
      </a>
      lost a major pipeline September 9 after a leak. As of September 19, the national average was up 2 cents to $2.20, though some areas, especially in the
      <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">
       Southeast
      </a>
      , saw increases of 20 to 30 cents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264">
       <a href="#cite_note-264">
        [264]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The pipeline returned to service after completion of a bypass on September 21.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265">
       <a href="#cite_note-265">
        [265]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On September 23, Brent crude fell slightly to $45.89 in anticipation of a September 26 OPEC meeting.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266">
       <a href="#cite_note-266">
        [266]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On September 29, West Texas Intermediate rose to $47.83 and Brent crude hit $49.24 after OPEC's decision to decrease production resulted in the biggest gains since April.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267">
       <a href="#cite_note-267">
        [267]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Oil ended September higher for the second month. With the dollar strong after improvement in the U.S. economy, and stock markets weak, West Texas Intermediate fell October 3 after reaching $48.87, the highest point since July 5. Brent crude fell after hitting $50.90, its highest in six weeks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268">
       <a href="#cite_note-268">
        [268]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On October 10, with Russia planning to join OPEC and Algeria saying others should, Brent crude reached its highest point in a year at $53.73, while West Texas Intermediate hit $51.60, the highest since June 9.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269">
       <a href="#cite_note-269">
        [269]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A week later, with supplies high and added U.S. production capacity, West Texas intermediate fell just below $50 and Brent crude ended the day at $51.16.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270">
       <a href="#cite_note-270">
        [270]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With lower inventories, on October 19 West Texas Intermediate reached $51.93, the highest since July 2015, while Brent crude reached $53.14.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271">
       <a href="#cite_note-271">
        [271]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
